{"parentUuid":"9a3214f5-7199-4f09-be37-469dc57a5995","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"c5a082e8-93b6-4004-947f-81487321ec46","agentId":"a03677c7f6601f388","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01LTEctTkRDsM6r6QdhfLc2u","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→import SwiftUI\n     2→\n     3→/// Centralized animation timing constants for mkdn.\n     4→///\n     5→/// Every animation in the application derives from named primitives defined here.\n     6→/// Each primitive traces back to the orb aesthetic -- the canonical animation\n     7→/// reference -- and is documented with its visual intent, design rationale, and\n     8→/// derivation.\n     9→///\n    10→/// ## Primitive Groups\n    11→///\n    12→/// - **Continuous**: ``breathe``, ``haloBloom`` -- repeating, sinusoidal, orb-derived\n    13→/// - **Spring**: ``springSettle``, ``gentleSpring``, ``quickSettle`` -- physical, bouncy\n    14→/// - **Fade**: ``fadeIn``, ``fadeOut``, ``crossfade``, ``quickFade`` -- opacity transitions\n    15→/// - **Orchestration**: ``staggerDelay``, ``staggerCap`` -- multi-element sequencing\n    16→/// - **Reduce Motion**: ``reducedCrossfade``, ``reducedInstant`` -- accessibility alternatives\n    17→enum AnimationConstants {\n    18→    // MARK: - Primitive: Breathe\n    19→\n    20→    // Continuous sinusoidal rhythm timed to human breathing (~12 cycles/min).\n    21→    // Derived from: orb core pulse. The foundational continuous animation.\n    22→\n    23→    /// Core breathing rhythm. 2.5s half-cycle = ~5s full cycle = ~12 cycles/min.\n    24→    ///\n    25→    /// - Visual intent: A gentle, living pulse that rises and falls like a resting breath.\n    26→    /// - Design rationale: ~12 cycles/min matches human resting respiratory rate, creating\n    27→    ///   a subconscious sense of calm. Sinusoidal easeInOut avoids mechanical feel.\n    28→    /// - Derivation: Foundational continuous primitive. The orb core pulse defines this\n    29→    ///   rhythm; all other continuous animations are timed relative to it.\n    30→    static let breathe: Animation = .easeInOut(duration: 2.5)\n    31→        .repeatForever(autoreverses: true)\n    32→\n    33→    /// Halo bloom: slightly slower than core breathing for dimensional offset.\n    34→    ///\n    35→    /// - Visual intent: An outer glow that expands and contracts behind the core pulse,\n    36→    ///   creating depth through phase offset.\n    37→    /// - Design rationale: 3.0s half-cycle vs 2.5s core creates a subtle phase drift\n    38→    ///   that makes the orb feel organic rather than mechanically synchronized.\n    39→    /// - Derivation: Variant of ``breathe``, slowed to create visual layering in the\n    40→    ///   orb's three-layer gradient structure.\n    41→    static let haloBloom: Animation = .easeInOut(duration: 3.0)\n    42→        .repeatForever(autoreverses: true)\n    43→\n    44→    // MARK: - Primitive: Spring-Settle\n    45→\n    46→    // Physical spring entrance with noticeable bounce. Used for prominent UI surfaces.\n    47→    // Derived from: orb appear. The orb \"bounces into existence.\"\n    48→\n    49→    /// Standard spring-settle for prominent entrances (overlays, focus borders).\n    50→    ///\n    51→    /// - Visual intent: A physical \"bounce into existence\" with noticeable but brief\n    52→    ///   overshoot.\n    53→    /// - Design rationale: Response 0.35 keeps entrance snappy; damping 0.7 allows one\n    54→    ///   visible bounce before settling, giving a sense of physical weight.\n    55→    /// - Derivation: Directly from the orb's appear animation translated to spring\n    56→    ///   physics. The orb \"breathes into existence\" -- this primitive captures that\n    57→    ///   entrance quality for non-orb UI surfaces.\n    58→    static let springSettle: Animation = .spring(\n    59→        response: 0.35,\n    60→        dampingFraction: 0.7\n    61→    )\n    62→\n    63→    // MARK: - Primitive: Gentle-Spring\n    64→\n    65→    // Softer spring with higher damping. Layout transitions that should feel physical\n    66→    // but not bouncy. Derived from: orb appear, dampened for subtlety.\n    67→\n    68→    /// Gentle spring for layout transitions (view mode switch, split pane).\n    69→    ///\n    70→    /// - Visual intent: A smooth, physical transition that feels weighted but not\n    71→    ///   bouncy. Content moves into place with momentum that decelerates naturally.\n    72→    /// - Design rationale: Response 0.4 gives slightly more time for spatial\n    73→    ///   transitions; damping 0.85 nearly eliminates overshoot, appropriate for layout\n    74→    ///   changes where bounce would feel distracting.\n    75→    /// - Derivation: ``springSettle`` dampened for subtlety. The orb's appear energy,\n    76→    ///   tamed for structural transitions that should feel solid rather than playful.\n    77→    static let gentleSpring: Animation = .spring(\n    78→        response: 0.4,\n    79→        dampingFraction: 0.85\n    80→    )\n    81→\n    82→    // MARK: - Primitive: Sidebar Slide\n    83→\n    84→    /// Smooth easeInOut slide for sidebar drawer animation.\n    85→    ///\n    86→    /// Uses a timing curve instead of a spring to guarantee zero overshoot.\n    87→    /// Even with continuous TextKit reflow (table row heights update on every\n    88→    /// frame via ``OverlayCoordinator/repositionOverlays()``), spring overshoot\n    89→    /// causes visible jitter as text reflows back and forth during bounce-back.\n    90→    /// An easeInOut curve decelerates smoothly into the final position with no\n    91→    /// directional reversal, producing a clean slide.\n    92→    static let sidebarSlide: Animation = .easeInOut(duration: 0.35)\n    93→\n    94→    // MARK: - Primitive: Quick-Settle\n    95→\n    96→    // Fast, crisp spring for micro-interactions. Minimal overshoot.\n    97→    // Derived from: orb spring, compressed for hover/feedback responsiveness.\n    98→\n    99→    /// Quick spring for hover feedback and micro-interactions.\n   100→    ///\n   101→    /// - Visual intent: A snappy response that registers as \"alive\" without drawing\n   102→    ///   attention. The element responds immediately and settles almost instantly.\n   103→    /// - Design rationale: Response 0.25 provides near-instant feedback; damping 0.8\n   104→    ///   minimizes overshoot so the interaction feels responsive, not wobbly.\n   105→    /// - Derivation: ``springSettle`` compressed in time and dampened for hover/feedback\n   106→    ///   contexts. Captures the orb's spring quality at micro-interaction scale.\n   107→    static let quickSettle: Animation = .spring(\n   108→        response: 0.25,\n   109→        dampingFraction: 0.8\n   110→    )\n   111→\n   112→    // MARK: - Primitive: Outline Pop\n   113→\n   114→    // Fast, snappy spring for the outline navigator morph. More bounce than\n   115→    // quickSettle to give the expand/collapse a \"poppy\" character.\n   116→    // Derived from: quickSettle, shortened and loosened for playful overlay UI.\n   117→\n   118→    /// Bouncy spring for the outline navigator expand morph.\n   119→    ///\n   120→    /// - Visual intent: The container inflates with visible overshoot, like a\n   121→    ///   rubber surface stretching open. Feels alive and physical.\n   122→    /// - Design rationale: Response 0.4 gives the expansion time to breathe;\n   123→    ///   damping 0.65 allows enough overshoot to feel elastic without wobbling.\n   124→    /// - Derivation: ``springSettle`` loosened for playful overlay UI.\n   125→    static let outlinePop: Animation = .spring(\n   126→        response: 0.4,\n   127→        dampingFraction: 0.65\n   128→    )\n   129→\n   130→    /// Firm easeOut for the outline navigator collapse layout change.\n   131→    ///\n   132→    /// Cannot undershoot — the breadcrumb size is a hard floor. The easeOut\n   133→    /// curve starts fast (releasing the rubber band) and decelerates firmly\n   134→    /// into the resting size.\n   135→    static let outlineClose: Animation = .easeOut(duration: 0.2)\n   136→\n   137→    /// Rubber band pull duration before the collapse releases.\n   138→    static let outlineStretchDuration: TimeInterval = 0.12\n   139→\n   140→    /// Delay before the landing bounce after collapse.\n   141→    static let outlineSettleDelay: TimeInterval = 0.19\n   142→\n   143→    /// Landing bounce spring after collapse — pops up then settles.\n   144→    static let outlineSettlePop: Animation = .spring(response: 0.15, dampingFraction: 0.4)\n   145→\n   146→    /// Return spring after landing bounce.\n   147→    static let outlineSettleReturn: Animation = .spring(response: 0.2, dampingFraction: 0.5)\n   148→\n   149→    /// Delay between landing pop and return.\n   150→    static let outlineSettleReturnDelay: TimeInterval = 0.08\n   151→\n   152→    /// Raw scroll-to-heading duration (seconds) for AppKit `NSAnimationContext`.\n   153→    ///\n   154→    /// Used by the outline navigator's scroll-to-heading animation in the\n   155→    /// ``SelectableTextView`` coordinator. Exposed as `CFTimeInterval` for\n   156→    /// AppKit compatibility (same pattern as ``fadeInDuration``).\n   157→    static let scrollToHeadingDuration: CFTimeInterval = 0.35\n   158→\n   159→    // MARK: - Primitive: Fade-In\n   160→\n   161→    // Smooth appearance. Ease-out curve (decelerates into rest).\n   162→    // Derived from: orb appear timing.\n   163→\n   164→    /// Raw fade-in duration (seconds) for use in Core Animation and AppKit contexts.\n   165→    ///\n   166→    /// Matches the duration of ``fadeIn``. Exposed as a `CFTimeInterval` so that\n   167→    /// ``EntranceAnimator`` cover-layer animations and ``OverlayCoordinator``\n   168→    /// overlay alpha animations can share the same timing without importing SwiftUI\n   169→    /// `Animation`.\n   170→    static let fadeInDuration: CFTimeInterval = 0.5\n   171→\n   172→    /// Standard fade-in for element appearance.\n   173→    ///\n   174→    /// - Visual intent: A smooth emergence from invisible to fully visible,\n   175→    ///   decelerating into rest so the element \"arrives\" gently.\n   176→    /// - Design rationale: 0.5s duration balances visibility (not too fast to miss)\n   177→    ///   with responsiveness (not so slow it feels sluggish). Ease-out curve\n   178→    ///   decelerates into the final state, matching the orb's gentle arrival.\n   179→    /// - Derivation: From the orb's appear timing. The orb fades in over 0.5s with\n   180→    ///   ease-out; this primitive generalizes that entrance for any element.\n   181→    static let fadeIn: Animation = .easeOut(duration: fadeInDuration)\n   182→\n   183→    // MARK: - Primitive: Fade-Out\n   184→\n   185→    // Smooth disappearance. Ease-in curve (accelerates away).\n   186→    // Derived from: orb dissolve timing.\n   187→\n   188→    /// Standard fade-out for element removal.\n   189→    ///\n   190→    /// - Visual intent: A smooth departure that accelerates away, giving a sense of\n   191→    ///   the element receding or dissolving rather than being abruptly cut.\n   192→    /// - Design rationale: 0.4s is slightly faster than fade-in (0.5s) because users\n   193→    ///   are less patient with exits than entrances. Ease-in curve accelerates away\n   194→    ///   from the current state, matching the orb's dissolve behavior.\n   195→    /// - Derivation: From the orb's dissolve timing. The orb's exit is a receding\n   196→    ///   fade; this primitive generalizes that departure for any element.\n   197→    static let fadeOut: Animation = .easeIn(duration: 0.4)\n   198→\n   199→    // MARK: - Primitive: Crossfade\n   200→\n   201→    // Symmetric blend between two states. Ease-in-out for balanced feel.\n   202→    // Derived from: theme transition aesthetic.\n   203→\n   204→    /// Crossfade for state transitions (theme change, loading to rendered).\n   205→    ///\n   206→    /// - Visual intent: A balanced blend between two states where neither entrance\n   207→    ///   nor exit dominates. Both states are equally weighted during the transition.\n   208→    /// - Design rationale: 0.35s is long enough to perceive as a transition (not a\n   209→    ///   glitch) but short enough to feel responsive. EaseInOut provides symmetry\n   210→    ///   between outgoing and incoming states.\n   211→    /// - Derivation: From the theme transition aesthetic. The crossfade bridges visual\n   212→    ///   states without the directional quality of fade-in/out, appropriate for\n   213→    ///   identity-changing transitions (color, content) rather than presence changes.\n   214→    static let crossfade: Animation = .easeInOut(duration: 0.35)\n   215→\n   216→    // MARK: - Primitive: Quick-Fade\n   217→\n   218→    // Fast fade for popover exit, transient feedback.\n   219→    // Derived from: crossfade, shortened for responsiveness.\n   220→\n   221→    /// Quick fade for responsive exits (popover dismiss, hover exit).\n   222→    ///\n   223→    /// - Visual intent: A fast, clean exit that feels immediate without being a hard\n   224→    ///   cut. The element is \"already going\" when the user notices the transition.\n   225→    /// - Design rationale: 0.2s is at the threshold of conscious perception -- fast\n   226→    ///   enough to feel instant, slow enough to avoid visual pop. Ease-out decelerates\n   227→    ///   into gone.\n   228→    /// - Derivation: ``crossfade`` shortened for responsiveness. Where crossfade\n   229→    ///   bridges two equal states, quick-fade prioritizes the destination over the\n   230→    ///   transition.\n   231→    static let quickFade: Animation = .easeOut(duration: 0.2)\n   232→\n   233→    // MARK: - Primitive: Quick-Shift\n   234→\n   235→    // Symmetric fast transition. Ease-in-out curve (balanced appear/disappear).\n   236→    // Derived from: crossfade, shortened for micro-transitions that need symmetry.\n   237→\n   238→    /// Quick symmetric transition for focus borders and state toggles.\n   239→    ///\n   240→    /// - Visual intent: A balanced, fast transition where appear and disappear\n   241→    ///   are equally weighted. The easeInOut curve gives a symmetric feel\n   242→    ///   appropriate for toggling states like focus borders.\n   243→    /// - Design rationale: 0.2s matches ``quickFade`` in duration but uses\n   244→    ///   easeInOut instead of easeOut, providing symmetry between on and off\n   245→    ///   states. Focus borders appear and disappear with equal emphasis.\n   246→    /// - Derivation: ``crossfade`` shortened to micro-transition speed. Where\n   247→    ///   ``quickFade`` prioritizes the exit, quickShift treats both directions\n   248→    ///   equally.\n   249→    static let quickShift: Animation = .easeInOut(duration: 0.2)\n   250→\n   251→    // MARK: - Orchestration: Stagger\n   252→\n   253→    /// Per-block stagger delay for content load entrance animation.\n   254→    ///\n   255→    /// - Visual intent: Successive content blocks appear in a fluid cascade, each\n   256→    ///   slightly after the previous, creating a \"reveal\" rather than an abrupt dump.\n   257→    /// - Design rationale: 30ms is fast enough that individual delays are not\n   258→    ///   consciously perceived, but the cumulative stagger creates a visible wave.\n   259→    /// - Derivation: Timed to complement ``fadeIn`` -- each block begins its 0.5s\n   260→    ///   fade-in 30ms after the previous, creating a smooth overlapping cascade.\n   261→    static let staggerDelay = 0.03\n   262→\n   263→    /// Maximum total stagger duration to cap entrance length on large documents.\n   264→    ///\n   265→    /// - Visual intent: Even with hundreds of blocks, the entrance sequence completes\n   266→    ///   within half a second. The document \"arrives\" promptly regardless of size.\n   267→    /// - Design rationale: 500ms cap means documents up to ~16 blocks get full\n   268→    ///   stagger; beyond that, remaining blocks share the tail of the window.\n   269→    static let staggerCap = 0.5\n   270→\n   271→    // MARK: - Entrance Gate\n   272→\n   273→    /// Maximum time to wait for viewport overlays to report their rendered size\n   274→    /// before dismissing the loading gate and starting the entrance cascade.\n   275→    ///\n   276→    /// - Design rationale: 2s balances user patience with slow-rendering Mermaid\n   277→    ///   diagrams. Most diagrams render within 1s; the timeout handles edge cases\n   278→    ///   (complex graphs, cold WebKit process pool) without leaving users staring\n   279→    ///   at a loading orb indefinitely.\n   280→    static let gateTimeout: TimeInterval = 2.0\n   281→\n   282→    // MARK: - Orb Rotation\n   283→\n   284→    /// Full rotation period for the orb's highlight orbit (seconds).\n   285→    static let orbRotationPeriod: TimeInterval = 8.0\n   286→\n   287→    // MARK: - Orb Colors\n   288→\n   289→    /// Solarized violet (#6c71c4) -- default handler prompt.\n   290→    /// Calm and mystical, chosen for its association with focus and intuition.\n   291→    static let orbDefaultHandlerColor = Color(red: 0.424, green: 0.443, blue: 0.769)\n   292→\n   293→    /// Solarized orange (#cb4b16) -- file changed on disk.\n   294→    /// A warm alert color signaling that attention is needed.\n   295→    static let orbFileChangedColor = Color(red: 0.796, green: 0.294, blue: 0.086)\n   296→\n   297→    /// Solarized base01 (#586e75) -- loading gate orb.\n   298→    /// Neutral grey-blue that reads as \"working\" without competing with the\n   299→    /// violet/orange status orb in the bottom-right corner.\n   300→    static let orbLoadingColor = Color(red: 0.345, green: 0.431, blue: 0.459)\n   301→\n   302→    // MARK: - Overlay Timing\n   303→\n   304→    /// How long the mode transition overlay remains visible before auto-dismiss.\n   305→    static let overlayDisplayDuration: Duration = .milliseconds(1_500)\n   306→\n   307→    /// Duration of the overlay fade-out (for scheduling cleanup after fade completes).\n   308→    static let overlayFadeOutDuration: Duration = .milliseconds(300)\n   309→\n   310→    // MARK: - Hover Feedback\n   311→\n   312→    /// Orb hover scale factor. Subtle enough to register subconsciously.\n   313→    ///\n   314→    /// - Visual intent: The orb \"notices\" the cursor -- a tiny, living response.\n   315→    /// - Design rationale: 1.06 is within the 1.05--1.08 range where scale changes\n   316→    ///   are felt rather than seen. Larger values risk feeling like a button press.\n   317→    /// - Derivation: Orb's living quality extended to cursor interaction. The orb\n   318→    ///   breathes; on hover, it also responds.\n   319→    static let hoverScaleFactor: CGFloat = 1.06\n   320→\n   321→    /// Toolbar button hover scale factor.\n   322→    ///\n   323→    /// - Visual intent: Toolbar items acknowledge the cursor with minimal motion.\n   324→    /// - Design rationale: 1.05 is slightly subtler than the orb (1.06) because\n   325→    ///   toolbar buttons are utilitarian, not expressive.\n   326→    /// - Derivation: ``hoverScaleFactor`` reduced for less expressive UI elements.\n   327→    static let toolbarHoverScale: CGFloat = 1.05\n   328→\n   329→    /// Mermaid diagram hover brightness overlay opacity.\n   330→    ///\n   331→    /// - Visual intent: An unfocused diagram brightens almost imperceptibly on hover,\n   332→    ///   hinting at interactivity without adding visual noise.\n   333→    /// - Design rationale: 0.03 opacity white overlay produces a brightness increase\n   334→    ///   that is subconsciously registered. Higher values look like a highlight; lower\n   335→    ///   values are invisible on most displays.\n   336→    /// - Derivation: Orb's glow aesthetic applied as a flat brightness layer,\n   337→    ///   appropriate for rectangular content areas.\n   338→    static let mermaidHoverBrightness = 0.03\n   339→\n   340→    // MARK: - Focus Border\n   341→\n   342→    /// Focus border stroke width at full visibility.\n   343→    ///\n   344→    /// - Visual intent: A clear but not heavy border that frames the focused diagram.\n   345→    /// - Design rationale: 2pt is the minimum width that reads clearly on Retina\n   346→    ///   displays while remaining elegant. Thicker borders feel heavy; thinner ones\n   347→    ///   disappear.\n   348→    /// - Derivation: Sized to complement ``focusGlowRadius`` -- the stroke provides\n   349→    ///   structure while the glow provides atmosphere.\n   350→    static let focusBorderWidth: CGFloat = 2.0\n   351→\n   352→    /// Focus border outer glow radius.\n   353→    ///\n   354→    /// - Visual intent: A soft halo behind the border that evokes the orb's glow,\n   355→    ///   visually connecting the focus state to the breathing orb aesthetic.\n   356→    /// - Design rationale: 6pt produces a visible but soft glow. The glow animates in\n   357→    ///   alongside the border via ``springSettle``.\n   358→    /// - Derivation: From the orb's halo bloom -- the focus glow is the orb's radiant\n   359→    ///   quality applied to a rectangular frame.\n   360→    static let focusGlowRadius: CGFloat = 6.0\n   361→\n   362→    // MARK: - Reduce Motion Alternatives\n   363→\n   364→    /// Short crossfade for Reduce Motion contexts.\n   365→    ///\n   366→    /// - Visual intent: Preserves continuity between states (no jarring hard cut)\n   367→    ///   while minimizing motion. The transition is felt as a brief blend.\n   368→    /// - Design rationale: 0.15s is fast enough that motion-sensitive users will not\n   369→    ///   experience discomfort, but slow enough to avoid the harsh feel of an instant\n   370→    ///   cut. Used for theme crossfade and state transitions with Reduce Motion.\n   371→    /// - Derivation: ``crossfade`` shortened to accessibility threshold. Preserves the\n   372→    ///   design intent (smooth state change) while respecting the user's preference.\n   373→    static let reducedCrossfade: Animation = .easeInOut(duration: 0.15)\n   374→\n   375→    /// Near-instant transition for Reduce Motion contexts where even a short crossfade\n   376→    /// is unnecessary.\n   377→    ///\n   378→    /// - Visual intent: Effectively instant, but technically animated to avoid SwiftUI\n   379→    ///   layout discontinuities that can occur with truly nil animations.\n   380→    /// - Design rationale: 0.01s is imperceptible. Using an explicit animation rather\n   381→    ///   than nil prevents potential layout jumpiness in some SwiftUI configurations.\n   382→    static let reducedInstant: Animation = .linear(duration: 0.01)\n   383→}\n   384→"}]},"uuid":"aef25018-209a-4676-bdf9-b7b9c7fe00f4","timestamp":"2026-03-24T21:25:53.167Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"9a3214f5-7199-4f09-be37-469dc57a5995","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/jud/Projects/mkdn","sessionId":"8b14ed92-1e72-4981-b2c7-95b4a078e6a6","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"main","slug":"adaptive-plotting-puzzle"}
{"parentUuid":"aef25018-209a-4676-bdf9-b7b9c7fe00f4","isSidechain":true,"agentId":"a03677c7f6601f388","message":{"model":"claude-opus-4-6","id":"msg_014xjXh7UHBghuZ8ULnR3nxZ","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"text","text":"I have now thoroughly explored every relevant file in the codebase. Here is the comprehensive design document.\n\n---\n\n# Table Rendering Rebuild: NSTextAttachmentViewProvider Architecture\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThe current table rendering system is a three-layer stack -- invisible inline text, SwiftUI visual overlay, NSView highlight overlay -- held together by a height negotiation loop, position index caching, selection highlight suppression, and dual-tracked column widths. It is the most complex subsystem in mkdn, responsible for at least 7 separate source files, 5 OverlayCoordinator extensions, and 3 CodeBlockBackgroundTextView extensions, all working to solve a single fundamental problem: making two independent layout systems (TextKit 2 paragraph styles and SwiftUI) agree on the pixel height of each table.\n\nThe new architecture replaces all of this with a single `NSTextAttachment` per table, using an `NSTextAttachmentViewProvider` to vend an `NSHostingView` wrapping the SwiftUI table. TextKit 2 asks the provider for the attachment's bounds; the provider computes them analytically from column widths and row heights. There is one source of truth. No negotiation. No invisible text. No overlay positioning. No selection highlight suppression. The SwiftUI view owns its own 2D selection model, find highlighting, and copy serialization.\n\nThe result is a system where roughly 1400 lines of overlay coordination, height negotiation, position indexing, selection suppression, and print-time NSBezierPath drawing are replaced by approximately 600 lines of clean, well-factored types with single responsibilities.\n\n---\n\n## Part 1: New Types\n\n### 1.1 `TableAttachmentViewProvider` (NSTextAttachmentViewProvider subclass)\n\n**File**: `mkdn/Core/Markdown/TableAttachmentViewProvider.swift`\n\n**Responsibility**: Vends the NSHostingView for a table attachment and computes its bounds analytically.\n\n**Key interfaces**:\n- `init(textAttachment:parentView:textLayoutManager:location:)` -- the standard TextKit 2 initializer. The attachment carries a `TableAttachmentData` payload.\n- `override func loadView()` -- creates an `NSHostingView<TableAttachmentView>` and assigns it to `self.view`. Passes the table data, theme, container width, and a binding for selection state.\n- `override func attachmentBounds(for attributes:location:textContainer:proposedLineFragment:position:)` -- computes the table's size analytically using `TableColumnSizer.computeWidths()` and `TableColumnSizer.estimateTableHeight()` against the text container's width. This is the single source of truth. No negotiation loop.\n\n**Design note**: The `proposedLineFragment` parameter gives us the container width at layout time. We use it directly in `TableColumnSizer.computeWidths()` to get exact column widths, then sum row heights (with padding) for the total height. The result is a `CGRect` with origin at `(0, descent-offset)` and the computed size. Because this is called by TextKit 2 during layout, the attachment always has the correct size for the current container width. Window resize triggers a layout pass, which calls `attachmentBounds` again with the new width. No manual observation needed.\n\n### 1.2 `TableAttachmentData` (struct, stored on the NSTextAttachment)\n\n**File**: `mkdn/Core/Markdown/TableAttachmentData.swift`\n\n**Responsibility**: Carries all table data needed by the view provider. Stored as `NSTextAttachment.contents` or a custom property via a small NSTextAttachment subclass.\n\n**Fields**:\n- `columns: [TableColumn]`\n- `rows: [[AttributedString]]`\n- `blockIndex: Int`\n- `tableRangeID: String` (UUID for identity)\n\n**Design note**: Since `NSTextAttachment.contents` expects `Data?`, we use a thin `TableTextAttachment: NSTextAttachment` subclass with a `var tableData: TableAttachmentData?` property. This is cleaner than encoding/decoding and follows the same pattern as the existing `NSObject`-based attribute values.\n\n### 1.3 `TableTextAttachment` (NSTextAttachment subclass)\n\n**File**: `mkdn/Core/Markdown/TableAttachmentData.swift` (same file, small type)\n\n**Responsibility**: Holds the `TableAttachmentData` payload and registers the view provider class.\n\n**Key detail**: In `init`, sets `self.allowsTextAttachmentView = true` and registers the view provider via the TextKit 2 `NSTextAttachment` API.\n\n### 1.4 `TableAttachmentView` (SwiftUI View)\n\n**File**: `mkdn/Features/Viewer/Views/TableAttachmentView.swift`\n\n**Responsibility**: The complete SwiftUI table rendering, including visual rendering, 2D selection, find highlighting, sticky header (internal scroll-aware), and copy support. This is the evolution of the current `TableBlockView`, but self-contained.\n\n**Sub-views** (private, within the same file):\n- `TableHeaderRow` -- replaces the current `TableHeaderView` as an internal component\n- `TableDataRow` -- renders a single data row\n- `TableCellView` -- renders a single cell with selection/find highlighting built in\n\n**Key interfaces**:\n- `@Observable` state class `TableSelectionState` -- holds the 2D selection model\n- `onSizeChange` callback for reporting actual rendered size back to the provider\n- Receives `containerWidth` from environment or binding\n\n### 1.5 `TableSelectionState` (@Observable class)\n\n**File**: `mkdn/Features/Viewer/Views/TableSelectionState.swift`\n\n**Responsibility**: Owns the 2D selection model for a single table.\n\n**Data types**:\n- `CellPosition` (reuse existing from `TableCellMap`)\n- `SelectionShape`: enum with cases `.none`, `.cells(Set<CellPosition>)`, `.rows(IndexSet)`, `.columns(IndexSet)`, `.rectangular(rows: Range<Int>, columns: Range<Int>)`, `.all`\n- `findMatches: Set<CellPosition>` -- cells containing find matches\n- `currentFindMatch: CellPosition?` -- the currently navigated-to find match\n\n**Gestures**:\n- Click on cell: select that cell\n- Click+drag: rubber-band rectangular selection\n- Shift+click: extend selection to rectangular region\n- Cmd+click: toggle individual cell\n- Click on row header area: select entire row\n- Click on column header: select entire column\n- Cmd+A when table is focused: select all cells\n\n**Design note**: This replaces `TableHighlightOverlay`, `TableCellMap.cellsInRange()`, and the `selectedCells` / `findHighlightCells` properties on the overlay. The selection is entirely within SwiftUI, not derived from NSTextView's character-level selection.\n\n### 1.6 `TableClipboardSerializer` (enum, static methods)\n\n**File**: `mkdn/Core/Markdown/TableClipboardSerializer.swift`\n\n**Responsibility**: Pure computation: takes a `SelectionShape`, column definitions, and row data, and produces pasteboard content.\n\n**Key methods**:\n- `static func tabDelimitedText(selection:columns:rows:) -> String`\n- `static func rtfData(selection:columns:rows:colors:) -> Data?`\n- `static func markdownText(selection:columns:rows:) -> String`\n\n**Design note**: This extracts the serialization logic currently split between `TableCellMap` (rtfData, tabDelimitedText) and `CodeBlockBackgroundTextView+TableCopy` (buildMixedClipboard, rtfTableRows, rtfParagraphs). The new type is a pure-computation uninhabitable enum, matching the project's pattern for stateless services (`TableColumnSizer`, `MarkdownRenderer`, `SyntaxHighlightEngine`).\n\n### 1.7 `TableFindAdapter` (struct)\n\n**File**: `mkdn/Features/Viewer/Views/TableFindAdapter.swift`\n\n**Responsibility**: Bridges the app-level find system to per-table find highlighting. Given a search query, searches the table's raw cell content and returns matching cell positions.\n\n**Key method**:\n- `static func findMatches(query: String, columns: [TableColumn], rows: [[AttributedString]], options: FindOptions) -> [CellPosition]`\n\n**Design note**: The current system searches the invisible text via NSTextView's find infrastructure, then maps character ranges back to cell positions. The new system searches the structured data directly, which is simpler and more correct (no risk of matching across cell boundaries on the invisible tab-separated text).\n\n---\n\n## Part 2: Existing Files to Modify\n\n### 2.1 `MarkdownTextStorageBuilder.swift`\n\n**What changes**: The `.table` case in `appendBlock()` switches from calling `appendTableInlineText()` to calling a new `appendTableAttachment()` method. This method creates a `TableTextAttachment` with a `TableAttachmentData` payload, wraps it in an `NSAttributedString(attachment:)`, applies the standard paragraph style, and appends an `AttachmentInfo` to the attachments array.\n\n**Key detail**: Tables now join mermaid, images, math, and thematic breaks in the `attachments` output rather than having their own `tableOverlays` output. The `TextStorageResult.tableOverlays` property becomes unnecessary. However, the `TextStorageResult` struct still needs to carry table identity information so the overlay coordinator can find them. The cleanest approach: `AttachmentInfo` already carries `blockIndex` and `block` (which for tables has `.table(columns, rows)`). The overlay coordinator can pattern-match on that.\n\n**The `isPrint` path**: When `isPrint: true`, the builder still needs to produce visible table text for print. Two options: (a) use the attachment approach and have the view provider render for print, or (b) keep the visible-text approach for print only. Option (a) is cleaner -- `NSPrintOperation` will render the attachment view. I recommend (a) as the primary path, with a fallback `drawTableContainers` only if testing reveals that TextKit 2's print pipeline does not render `NSTextAttachmentViewProvider` views. This needs empirical validation during implementation.\n\n### 2.2 `MarkdownTextStorageBuilder.swift` (the `TextStorageResult` struct)\n\n**What changes**: Remove the `tableOverlays` property. Tables are now in `attachments`.\n\nThis is a public API change for mkdnLib. The `TableOverlayInfo` type becomes unused.\n\n### 2.3 `SelectableTextView.swift`\n\n**What changes**:\n- Remove `tableOverlays` from the struct's stored properties\n- Remove the `tableOverlays:` parameter from `refreshOverlays()`\n- Remove the `coordinator.overlayCoordinator.updateTableOverlays(...)` call\n- Remove the `selectionDragHandler` wiring (table selection is now internal to the SwiftUI view, not derived from NSTextView selection ranges)\n- Register the `TableAttachmentViewProvider` with the `NSTextContentStorage` in `makeNSView()` via `textContentStorage.register(TableAttachmentViewProvider.self, forContentType:)` or by setting `NSTextAttachment.textAttachmentViewProviderClass`\n\n**Key detail**: The registration of the view provider is the critical new step. TextKit 2 on macOS 14+ supports `NSTextAttachmentViewProvider`. The provider is registered globally on the attachment class, not per-instance.\n\n### 2.4 `OverlayCoordinator.swift`\n\n**What changes**:\n- Remove all table-specific properties: `tableRangeIndex`, `pendingVisualHeights`, and the table-related fields from `OverlayEntry` (`tableRangeID`, `highlightOverlay`, `cellMap`, `lastAppliedVisualHeight`)\n- `OverlayEntry` simplifies to just `view`, `attachment`, `block`, `preferredWidth`\n- `repositionOverlays()` no longer needs `shouldPositionEntry` filtering or `reconcileLayoutThroughViewport` (tables were the only reason for the reconciliation loop -- they were the only overlays that had text-range-based positioning)\n- Remove `stickyHeaders` dictionary (sticky headers become internal to `TableAttachmentView`)\n\n### 2.5 `OverlayCoordinator+Positioning.swift`\n\n**What changes**:\n- Remove `positionEntry`'s table branch (`if entry.tableRangeID != nil`)\n- Simplify to only handle attachment-based positioning\n\n### 2.6 `CodeBlockBackgroundTextView.swift`\n\n**What changes**:\n- Remove `cachedTableRanges`, `isTableRangeCacheValid`\n- Remove `selectionDragHandler`\n- Remove the `handleTableCopy()` call from `copy(_:)`\n- Remove `eraseTableSelectionHighlights(in:)` call from `draw(_:)`\n- Remove `drawTableContainers(in:)` call from `drawBackground(in:)`\n- Remove `invalidateCodeBlockCache()`'s table range invalidation\n\n### 2.7 `EntranceAnimator.swift`\n\n**What changes**:\n- Remove `tableDelays` dictionary\n- Remove the `\"table-\"` prefix handling in `blockGroupID()` and `processBlockGroups()`\n- Tables will be handled like other attachments: the `recordAttachmentDelay` method already handles `.attachment` attributes, and since tables are now attachments, they get entrance delays automatically\n\n### 2.8 `OverlayCoordinator+EntranceAnimation.swift`\n\n**What changes**:\n- Remove the `tableDelays` branch from `applyEntranceAnimation()`. Tables are now regular attachments and use `attachmentDelays`.\n\n### 2.9 `OverlayCoordinator+PositionIndex.swift`\n\n**What changes**:\n- Remove the `tableRangeIndex` dictionary and its `enumerateAttribute(TableAttributes.range, ...)` scan. Only the `attachmentIndex` scan remains (and tables are now found there).\n\n### 2.10 `OverlayCoordinator+Observation.swift`\n\n**What changes**:\n- Remove the entire sticky header logic from `handleScrollBoundsChange()` (sticky headers are now internal to `TableAttachmentView`)\n- Remove `stickyHeaderHeight()` method\n- The scroll observer still fires for overlay repositioning, but the table-specific code is gone\n\n### 2.11 `MarkdownPreviewView.swift`\n\n**What changes**: Remove `tableOverlays` from any place it is threaded through to `SelectableTextView`.\n\n### 2.12 `FindState.swift` / `SelectableTextView+Coordinator.swift`\n\n**What changes**: The coordinator's `handleFindUpdate()` currently calls `overlayCoordinator.updateTableFindHighlights(matchRanges:currentIndex:)`. This call is removed. Instead, find integration works through the `TableFindAdapter` which is called by the `TableAttachmentView` when it observes find state changes from the environment.\n\n---\n\n## Part 3: Files and Code to Delete\n\n### 3.1 Entire Files to Delete\n\n| File | Reason |\n|------|--------|\n| `mkdn/Core/Markdown/MarkdownTextStorageBuilder+TableInline.swift` | The entire invisible text generation approach is removed. All 275 lines. |\n| `mkdn/Core/Markdown/TableCellMap.swift` | The character-offset-to-cell mapping is no longer needed. Cell identity is structural (row, column), not character-offset-based. 280 lines. |\n| `mkdn/Core/Markdown/TableAttributes.swift` | The custom NSAttributedString keys (`mkdn.tableRange`, `mkdn.tableCellMap`, `mkdn.tableColors`, `mkdn.tableIsHeader`) are no longer applied to text storage. 66 lines. |\n| `mkdn/Features/Viewer/Views/TableBlockView.swift` | Replaced by `TableAttachmentView`. 148 lines. |\n| `mkdn/Features/Viewer/Views/TableHeaderView.swift` | Replaced by `TableHeaderRow` internal to `TableAttachmentView`. 54 lines. |\n| `mkdn/Features/Viewer/Views/TableHighlightOverlay.swift` | Replaced by inline selection/find highlighting in `TableAttachmentView`. 144 lines. |\n| `mkdn/Features/Viewer/Views/OverlayCoordinator+TableOverlays.swift` | All table overlay creation, text-range positioning, selection routing, and find highlight routing. 411 lines. |\n| `mkdn/Features/Viewer/Views/OverlayCoordinator+TableHeights.swift` | The entire height negotiation system. 317 lines. |\n| `mkdn/Features/Viewer/Views/CodeBlockBackgroundTextView+TableSelection.swift` | Selection highlight suppression no longer needed. 131 lines. |\n| `mkdn/Features/Viewer/Views/CodeBlockBackgroundTextView+TableCopy.swift` | Table-aware copy logic. Replaced by `TableClipboardSerializer` called from within `TableAttachmentView`. 266 lines. |\n| `mkdn/Features/Viewer/Views/CodeBlockBackgroundTextView+TablePrint.swift` | Print-time NSBezierPath table drawing. The attachment view provider handles print rendering. 244 lines. |\n\n### 3.2 Specific Types to Delete\n\n- `TableOverlayInfo` struct in `MarkdownTextStorageBuilder.swift` -- the `tableOverlays` output channel is removed\n- `TableRowContext` struct in `MarkdownTextStorageBuilder+TableInline.swift` -- part of the deleted file\n- `TableColorInfo` class in `TableAttributes.swift` -- part of the deleted file. Theme colors are now resolved within the SwiftUI view from `AppSettings` via environment, not carried as NSAttributedString attributes.\n- `PassthroughHostingView` in `OverlayCoordinator+TableOverlays.swift` -- only used for table overlays. (If it is also used for other overlays, check; but from the code, the attachment overlays use regular `NSHostingView`, only table overlays used `PassthroughHostingView`.)\n\n### 3.3 Specific Methods/Extensions to Delete\n\n- `OverlayCoordinator.updateTableOverlays(...)` \n- `OverlayCoordinator.updateTableSelections(...)`\n- `OverlayCoordinator.updateTableFindHighlights(...)`\n- `OverlayCoordinator.adjustTableRowHeights(...)`\n- `OverlayCoordinator.applyVisualHeight(...)`\n- `OverlayCoordinator.distributeHeights(...)`\n- `OverlayCoordinator.correctedGeometry(...)`\n- `OverlayCoordinator.wrappedRowHeight(...)`\n- `OverlayCoordinator.applyRowHeights(...)`\n- `OverlayCoordinator.invalidateTableLayout(...)`\n- `OverlayCoordinator.positionTextRangeEntry(...)`\n- `OverlayCoordinator.boundingRect(for:context:)`\n- `OverlayCoordinator.findTableTextRange(for:)`\n- `CodeBlockBackgroundTextView.eraseTableSelectionHighlights(in:)`\n- `CodeBlockBackgroundTextView.handleTableCopy()`\n- `CodeBlockBackgroundTextView.drawTableContainers(in:)`\n- `MarkdownTextStorageBuilder.appendTableInlineText(...)`\n- `MarkdownTextStorageBuilder.buildTableTabStops(...)`\n- `MarkdownTextStorageBuilder.estimateInlineRowHeight(...)`\n\n### 3.4 Test Files to Rewrite\n\n- `mkdnTests/Unit/Core/MarkdownTextStorageBuilderTableTests.swift` -- rewrite for attachment-based output\n- `mkdnTests/Unit/Core/TableCellMapTests.swift` -- delete entirely (type is removed)\n- `mkdnTests/Unit/Core/TableAttributesTests.swift` -- delete entirely (type is removed)\n\n---\n\n## Part 4: The Rendering Pipeline\n\n### Step 1: Parsing (unchanged)\n\n`MarkdownVisitor.convertTable()` produces `MarkdownBlock.table(columns:rows:)`. No change.\n\n### Step 2: Text Storage Building\n\n`MarkdownTextStorageBuilder.appendBlock()` dispatches `.table` to a new `appendTableAttachment()`:\n\n1. Create a `TableTextAttachment` with `tableData = TableAttachmentData(columns, rows, blockIndex, UUID)`\n2. Set initial bounds via `TableColumnSizer.computeWidths()` at `defaultEstimationContainerWidth` (600pt) plus `TableColumnSizer.estimateTableHeight()` -- this gives TextKit 2 a reasonable initial size before `attachmentBounds` is called with the actual container width\n3. Wrap in `NSAttributedString(attachment:)` with paragraph style (blockSpacing)\n4. Append to `attachments` array as `AttachmentInfo`\n\n### Step 3: TextKit 2 Layout\n\nWhen `NSTextLayoutManager` encounters the attachment during layout:\n1. It calls `TableAttachmentViewProvider.attachmentBounds(for:location:textContainer:proposedLineFragment:position:)` \n2. The provider reads `proposedLineFragment.width` as the container width\n3. Calls `TableColumnSizer.computeWidths()` with that width\n4. Calls height estimation for each row at those column widths\n5. Returns `CGRect(x: 0, y: descent, width: totalWidth, height: totalHeight)`\n6. TextKit 2 allocates exactly that space in the layout\n\n### Step 4: View Vending\n\nTextKit 2 calls `loadView()` on the provider:\n1. Provider creates `TableAttachmentView` with the columns, rows, and blockIndex\n2. Wraps in `NSHostingView`\n3. Injects `AppSettings` and any needed environment\n4. Assigns to `self.view`\n\n### Step 5: Visual Rendering\n\n`TableAttachmentView` renders identically to the current `TableBlockView`: VStack of header row + divider + data rows, with rounded rect border, zebra striping, and column alignment. The SwiftUI view is sized by TextKit 2 to the bounds returned by `attachmentBounds`.\n\n**Resize handling**: When the window resizes, TextKit 2 re-layouts, calls `attachmentBounds` with the new `proposedLineFragment`, gets updated bounds, re-sizes the hosting view, and `TableAttachmentView` re-renders with the new column widths. No manual observation, no convergence loop, no height distribution.\n\n---\n\n## Part 5: The Selection Model\n\n### Data Types\n\n```\nSelectionShape:\n  .none\n  .cells(Set<CellPosition>)\n  .rows(IndexSet)\n  .columns(IndexSet)\n  .rectangular(rows: Range<Int>, columns: Range<Int>)\n  .all\n```\n\n`CellPosition` stays as `(row: Int, column: Int)` with `row == -1` for header, matching the existing convention.\n\n### Gesture Handling\n\nThe `TableAttachmentView` applies gesture recognizers:\n\n- **Single click on cell**: `.cells([position])`. The hosting view does NOT return nil from `hitTest` (unlike the current `PassthroughHostingView`). The table owns its own interaction.\n- **Click+drag**: Computes the rectangular bounding box of the drag start and current position, selects all cells in that rectangle as `.rectangular(...)`.\n- **Shift+click**: Extends the current selection to include the clicked cell, forming a `.rectangular(...)` from the bounding box of the old selection and the new click.\n- **Cmd+click**: Toggles the clicked cell in/out of a `.cells(...)` selection.\n- **Click on column header**: `.columns([colIndex])`. Cmd+click toggles.\n- **Click on row number area** (if rendered): `.rows([rowIndex])`.\n- **Cmd+A** when table has focus: `.all`.\n- **Escape**: `.none`, resign focus.\n\n### Visual Feedback\n\nSelection highlighting is rendered inline in `TableCellView` as a background layer. Each cell checks `selectionState.isSelected(row:column:)` and applies the accent color at 0.3 alpha if selected. No separate overlay view needed.\n\nFind highlighting works the same way: each cell checks `selectionState.isFindMatch(row:column:)` and `selectionState.isCurrentFindMatch(row:column:)`.\n\n### Copy Serialization\n\nWhen the user presses Cmd+C while a table has focus and a non-empty selection:\n1. `TableAttachmentView` intercepts the copy command via `.onCopyCommand`\n2. Calls `TableClipboardSerializer.tabDelimitedText(selection:columns:rows:)` for plain text\n3. Calls `TableClipboardSerializer.rtfData(selection:columns:rows:colors:)` for RTF\n4. Places both on `NSPasteboard.general`\n\nWhen the user selects text spanning a paragraph, a table attachment, and another paragraph, and presses Cmd+C: the standard NSTextView copy produces an attributed string that includes the attachment. The attachment's textual representation (from `NSTextAttachment`'s built-in text extraction) provides the plain text fallback. We override this by providing a `NSTextAttachmentViewProvider.textRepresentation` that returns the table's tab-delimited content. This gives correct paste-as-text behavior for mixed selections.\n\n---\n\n## Part 6: Find-in-Page Integration\n\n### How Matches Are Found\n\n`TableFindAdapter.findMatches(query:columns:rows:options:)` performs a direct string search on each cell's plain text content. Returns `[CellPosition]` for all cells containing a match.\n\nThis is called by `TableAttachmentView` when it observes `FindState.query` changes through the environment.\n\n### How Matches Are Highlighted\n\n`TableSelectionState.findMatches` is set to the result of `TableFindAdapter.findMatches()`. Each `TableCellView` checks this set and applies the find highlight color (yellow at 0.15 alpha for passive matches, 0.4 alpha for the current match).\n\n### How Matches Are Navigated\n\n`FindState` carries a `currentIndex` and the total match array. For tables, the find system needs to know how many matches are in each table and which cells they correspond to. The adapter returns a count; `FindState` uses this to navigate through matches. When the current match falls within a table:\n1. `FindState.currentIndex` maps to a specific table and cell position\n2. `TableAttachmentView` observes the current match index and sets `selectionState.currentFindMatch`\n3. If the match cell is offscreen, the table scrolls to reveal it (or the outer scroll view scrolls to show the table)\n\n**Integration approach**: Each `TableAttachmentView` registers its find match count and positions with a shared find coordinator. This is lighter than the current approach of intersecting NSRange arrays with table character ranges.\n\n---\n\n## Part 7: Print Support\n\n### Primary Approach\n\n`NSTextAttachmentViewProvider` views are rendered by TextKit 2 during print operations. The `TableAttachmentView` should render correctly in the print pipeline if:\n1. The hosting view is resolvable during print layout\n2. Theme colors are switched to `PrintPalette` during the print build\n\nThe existing `CodeBlockBackgroundTextView.printView(_:)` rebuilds the attributed string with `isPrint: true`. In the new system, this rebuild creates `TableTextAttachment` instances just like the screen path. The `TableAttachmentViewProvider` detects the print context (via `NSPrintOperation.current != nil` or a flag on the attachment data) and uses `PrintPalette` colors.\n\n### Fallback Approach\n\nIf empirical testing shows that `NSTextAttachmentViewProvider` views do not render in the print pipeline (this is a known limitation in some TextKit 2 configurations), the fallback is:\n1. When `isPrint: true`, use the current `appendTableInlineText` approach (visible text, no overlay)\n2. Keep `drawTableContainers` for print only\n\nThis would mean retaining `MarkdownTextStorageBuilder+TableInline.swift` and `CodeBlockBackgroundTextView+TablePrint.swift` with `#if` guards or isPrint-only code paths. But I expect the primary approach to work on macOS 14+.\n\n---\n\n## Part 8: Theme Integration\n\n`TableAttachmentView` reads `AppSettings` from the SwiftUI environment (injected by the provider's `loadView()`). When the theme changes:\n1. `AppSettings.themeMode` updates\n2. SwiftUI re-renders `TableAttachmentView` with new colors\n3. No manual invalidation needed\n\nThis is substantially simpler than the current system where theme changes require rebuilding the entire attributed string (because `TableColorInfo` is baked into the attributes) and the overlay coordinator must rebuild overlays.\n\n**Caveat**: The `NSTextAttachmentViewProvider` creates the hosting view once in `loadView()`. Environment changes must propagate to the hosting view. The provider should hold a weak reference to the hosting view and update its root view when theme changes occur, or (simpler) inject `AppSettings` as an `@Observable` environment value, which SwiftUI will observe automatically.\n\n---\n\n## Part 9: Entrance Animation\n\n### Current System\n\n`EntranceAnimator` groups table fragments by `TableAttributes.range` and creates a full-width cover layer. `OverlayCoordinator` applies alpha animation delays to table overlay views.\n\n### New System\n\nTables are now attachments. The `EntranceAnimator` already handles attachments via `recordAttachmentDelay()`. Tables will automatically get entrance delays based on their Y position, just like mermaid diagrams and images do today.\n\nThe `blockGroupID()` method's table branch (checking `TableAttributes.range`) is removed. The attachment branch (checking `.attachment`) already handles `TableTextAttachment` instances.\n\nThe `tableDelays` dictionary is removed from `EntranceAnimator` and `OverlayCoordinator+EntranceAnimation`. Tables use `attachmentDelays` instead.\n\n---\n\n## Part 10: Migration Path\n\n### Can This Be Done Incrementally?\n\nYes, but with a clear switchover point. The key insight is that the table rendering pipeline has a clean boundary at the `MarkdownTextStorageBuilder.appendBlock()` dispatch. The `.table` case currently calls `appendTableInlineText()`; changing it to call `appendTableAttachment()` is the single switch.\n\n### Recommended Sequence\n\n**Phase 1: Foundation (can merge independently)**\n1. Create `TableTextAttachment` and `TableAttachmentData` -- pure data types with no behavioral coupling\n2. Create `TableClipboardSerializer` -- extract and test the serialization logic from `TableCellMap` and `CodeBlockBackgroundTextView+TableCopy`\n3. Create `TableFindAdapter` -- pure function, easily testable\n4. Create `TableSelectionState` -- pure state model, testable without UI\n\n**Phase 2: The View (can merge independently)**\n5. Create `TableAttachmentView` -- initially as a standalone SwiftUI view that can be previewed in isolation. This is the evolution of `TableBlockView` with selection and find highlighting built in. Test with SwiftUI previews.\n\n**Phase 3: The Provider (the switchover)**\n6. Create `TableAttachmentViewProvider` with `attachmentBounds()` and `loadView()`\n7. Add `appendTableAttachment()` to `MarkdownTextStorageBuilder`\n8. Switch the `.table` dispatch in `appendBlock()` from `appendTableInlineText` to `appendTableAttachment`\n9. Register the provider in `SelectableTextView.makeNSView()`\n10. Remove `tableOverlays` from `TextStorageResult`, `SelectableTextView`, and the overlay coordinator call chain\n\n**Phase 4: Cleanup (the deletions)**\n11. Delete the 11 files listed in Part 3.1\n12. Remove the methods listed in Part 3.3\n13. Simplify `OverlayCoordinator` and `CodeBlockBackgroundTextView`\n14. Rewrite table tests\n\n**Phase 5: Polish**\n15. Verify print rendering (and implement fallback if needed)\n16. Visual testing with all fixtures in both themes\n17. Test find-in-page integration\n18. Test mixed copy (paragraph + table + paragraph)\n19. Test entrance animation timing\n\n### Risk Points\n\n1. **NSTextAttachmentViewProvider print rendering**: This is the biggest unknown. If TextKit 2 does not render provider-vended views during print, we need the fallback (retain visible-text approach for print only). Validate early in Phase 3.\n\n2. **attachmentBounds accuracy**: If `proposedLineFragment.width` does not match the actual container width, column widths will be wrong. Validate that `proposedLineFragment` gives the correct width in all cases (initial layout, resize, print).\n\n3. **NSTextView selection across attachments**: When the user drags a selection from a paragraph through a table attachment to the next paragraph, does NSTextView's selection model include the attachment character? The table needs to decide: should it show its internal selection when the NSTextView selection includes the attachment character? This needs careful UX design.\n\n4. **Focus model**: The table now intercepts mouse events (no `PassthroughHostingView`). This means clicking inside a table does not position the NSTextView insertion point. The UX needs to handle the boundary between \"I'm interacting with the table\" and \"I'm selecting text in the document.\" A reasonable model: clicking inside the table focuses the table (selection is internal); clicking outside the table or pressing Escape returns focus to the document text view.\n\n5. **iOS impact**: The iOS table rendering (`TableBlockViewiOS.swift`) is unaffected -- it already uses a native SwiftUI grid with `TableColumnSizer`. The shared types (`TableColumn`, `TableColumnAlignment`, `TableColumnSizer`) are unchanged. However, `TableCellMap` is currently public API in mkdnLib. Its removal is a breaking change for any consumer using it. If this is a concern, deprecate rather than delete and remove in a subsequent release.\n\n---\n\n## What Makes This Elegant\n\n**Single source of truth for geometry.** The current system has column widths tracked in four places (tab stops, overlay frames, cellMap, highlight overlay scaling) and row heights negotiated between two layout systems. The new system computes geometry once in `attachmentBounds()` and TextKit 2 propagates it everywhere.\n\n**No convergence loops.** The 2pt threshold convergence guard, the `distributeHeights` proportional distribution, the `lastAppliedVisualHeight` state -- all artifacts of having two layout systems that must agree. Gone.\n\n**Selection is structural, not character-mapped.** The current system maps NSTextView character offsets to cell positions via binary search on sorted entries. The new system has direct (row, column) addressing. No character ranges, no offset calculations, no off-by-one risks on cell boundaries.\n\n**The table is a self-contained unit.** Visual rendering, selection, find highlighting, copy serialization, and sticky headers are all within `TableAttachmentView`. To understand how tables work, you read one file. The current system requires reading 11 files across 3 architectural layers.\n\n**Theme changes are free.** SwiftUI observation handles theme propagation. No attributed string rebuild, no overlay teardown/rebuild, no color info carrier classes stored as NSObject subclasses in attributed string attributes.\n\n**The overlay coordinator gets simpler.** Removing tables from the overlay coordinator eliminates 728+ lines across 3 extension files, the reconciliation loop, the sticky header logic, and the `tableRangeIndex`. What remains is a clean attachment-positioning coordinator for mermaid, images, math, and thematic breaks.\n\n---\n\n### Critical Files for Implementation\n- `/Users/jud/Projects/mkdn/mkdn/Core/Markdown/MarkdownTextStorageBuilder.swift` - Central dispatch point: the `.table` case in `appendBlock()` switches from invisible text to attachment, and `TextStorageResult` loses `tableOverlays`\n- `/Users/jud/Projects/mkdn/mkdn/Features/Viewer/Views/SelectableTextView.swift` - Provider registration site in `makeNSView()` and removal of `tableOverlays` threading\n- `/Users/jud/Projects/mkdn/mkdn/Features/Viewer/Views/OverlayCoordinator.swift` - Heaviest simplification: all table-specific properties, entry fields, and coordination logic removed from the central coordinator and its 2 table extension files\n- `/Users/jud/Projects/mkdn/mkdn/Features/Viewer/Views/TableBlockView.swift` - Existing SwiftUI table rendering to evolve into `TableAttachmentView` (reuse visual structure, add selection/find/copy/sticky-header)\n- `/Users/jud/Projects/mkdn/mkdn/Core/Markdown/TableColumnSizer.swift` - Retained unchanged as the pure-computation engine called from `attachmentBounds()` -- understanding its API is essential for the provider implementation"}],"stop_reason":"end_turn","stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":1,"cache_creation_input_tokens":7039,"cache_read_input_tokens":108688,"output_tokens":9015,"server_tool_use":{"web_search_requests":0,"web_fetch_requests":0},"service_tier":"standard","cache_creation":{"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":7039},"inference_geo":"","iterations":[],"speed":"standard"}},"requestId":"req_011CZNcSXp4Gk3nx1JmD6gj2","type":"assistant","uuid":"c43e29b7-719f-4088-8810-a868b9d18c41","timestamp":"2026-03-24T21:29:15.242Z","userType":"external","entrypoint":"cli","cwd":"/Users/jud/Projects/mkdn","sessionId":"8b14ed92-1e72-4981-b2c7-95b4a078e6a6","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"main","slug":"adaptive-plotting-puzzle"}
